## Why This Stack at Your Scale

### Why SonarCloud over GitHub Native Coverage?
• Portfolio dashboard: See coverage across all 250
  repos in one view
• Inline PR comments: Actual code-level analysis, not
  just %
• Quality gates: Block merge if coverage drops AND
  new bugs introduced
• Security hotspots: Beyond coverage — actual
  vulnerability analysis
• Free for OSS: No billing risk like Codecov

### Why CircleCI over GitHub Actions?
• Per-repo billing: No org-level exhaustion — each
  repo has its own minutes
• Generous free tier: 6,000 min/month (GitHub gives
  2,000 for private repos)
• Native Docker layer caching: Faster Rust builds
• GitHub + GitLab + Bitbucket: Single CI platform for
  all three

### Why Woodpecker for GitLab/Bitbucket?
• GitHub Actions-compatible syntax (mostly)
• Self-hosted: No per-minute billing
• Forgejo/Gitea compatible: Your hybrid setup
• Plugin ecosystem: Rust, Go, Docker, notifications

───────────────────────────────────────────────────

6. Render - Free tier for static sites
7. Fly.io - 3 small VMs free
8. Hetzner - €3.50/month ($4) for 2 cores, 4GB RAM -
   NOT free but extremely cheap
9. Kimsufi/OVH - $10-15/month servers
10. DigitalOcean - $4/month droplets (1GB RAM, 25GB
    SSD)
11. Vultr - $2.50/month (768MB RAM)

$20/month flat rate options for their needs:

At $20/month, they could get substantial infrastructure:
• Hetzner: €17.90/month (about $19.50) = 4 cores, 8GB
  RAM, 160GB NVMe
    ◦ Excellent for self-hosted runners
    ◦ EU or US location
    ◦ Great value but no free tier

• DigitalOcean: $20/month = 4GB RAM, 80GB SSD, 4
  vCPUs
    ◦ Simple, reliable
    ◦ One-click Docker/CI apps

• Vultr: $20/month = 4GB RAM, 80GB SSD, 3 vCPUs
    ◦ Global locations
    ◦ Block storage cheap

• Linode: $20/month = 4GB RAM, 80GB SSD, 4 vCPUs (now
  Akamai)

Oracle Cloud Free Tier is really the standout here - they get 2 free VMs perpetually with 1GB RAM and 200GB storage each. This is substantial for running persistent self-hosted runners and artifact storage without any monthly cost.

For the $20 flat-rate option, Hetzner offers the best specs at that price point - around $19.50 gets them 4 cores, 8GB RAM, and 160GB NVMe storage. They could also deploy Oracle Cloud's always-free VMs alongside this to distribute the workload, then scale to Hetzner if they need more horsepower. The setup would involve spinning up 2-4 self-hosted GitHub runners, installing Woodpecker CI on one of the instances, provisioning a SonarQube instance for code quality scanning, and allocating one machine as a persistent deployment server.

The constraints they're working with are tight though - at $20/month they're looking at roughly 4 cores, 8-16GB RAM, and 80-160GB storage, which means running a full SonarQube instance alongside multiple runners could get memory-constrained pretty quickly. Oracle's free tier becomes really attractive here since they could dedicate one always-free instance to the most resource-intensive tasks and use the $20/month server for the heavier workloads.

This is exactly the right question. Let me do a proper analysis of free/cheap VPS for self-hosted CI at your scale.

## Most Robust Option: Oracle Cloud (Free) +

## Hetzner ($20)

### Why This Combo?

1. Oracle's 200GB storage = massive artifact cache
   (Docker layers, coverage reports, Snyk DB)
2. Hetzner's NVMe = fast ephemeral CI builds
3. No single point of failure = Oracle + Hetzner are
   separate providers
4. $20 total = well under your budget
5. Scales up = when you need more, add another Hetzner
   or move to Oracle's paid tier

### Setup Path

# Oracle Cloud (free forever)
# 1. Sign up: cloud.oracle.com (verify phone +
  credit card)
# 2. Create Ampere instance: 4GB RAM, 200GB SSD
  , Ubuntu 22.04
# 3. Install: SonarQube + PostgreSQL + Nginx re
  verse proxy

# Hetzner €17.90/mo (~$20)
# 1. Sign up: hetzner.com (pay with PayPal/card
  )
# 2. Deploy Ubuntu 22.04, add SSH key
# 3. Install Woodpecker CI server + agents
# 4. Register as GitHub Actions self-hosted run
  ner

# Total: $0 (Oracle) + $20 (Hetzner) = $20/mo

### What You Get

• 100-200 CI jobs/day across Oracle + Hetzner runners
• SonarQube for deep code analysis (Oracle)
• Woodpecker for GitLab/Bitbucket + overflow GitHub
  CI (Hetzner)
• Persistent deploys via Docker Compose on Hetzner
• Artifact storage on Oracle's 200GB
• Nightly Snyk scans via Hetzner (bypasses GitHub
  Actions billing entirely)

───────────────────────────────────────────────────


## Alternative: All-In on $20 Hetzner

If Oracle approval is too annoying, just use Hetzner alone:

$20/mo Hetzner (4 cores, 16GB RAM, 160GB NVMe):
├─ 1x Woodpecker CI server
├─ 2x Woodpecker CI agents (ephemeral Docker)
├─ 1x GitHub Actions runner (small jobs)
├─ SonarScanner CLI (no full SonarQube, just sc
  anner)
└─ Snyk CLI + artifact storage

This handles 50-100 CI jobs/day. For 100-500 PRs/day at full scale, you'd need 2-3 Hetzner servers ($40-60/mo) or add Oracle free tier.

───────────────────────────────────────────────────


## My Recommendation

Oracle Cloud (free) + Hetzner ($20) — total $20/mo:

1. Oracle for persistence: SonarQube + artifact
   storage + one runner
2. Hetzner for compute: Woodpecker + 3 ephemeral
   agents + Snyk

This gives you:
• No GitHub Actions billing exhaustion
• Full SonarQube analysis
• Persistent deploys
• 100-300 CI jobs/day capacity
• Room to scale by adding another Hetzner at $20

● [20:23:34] Finished e8697da1-53ad-4f4a-b8d4-5c7f9dd7f9d0
FORGE repos main       [v2.3.2/minimax-m2.7/844690]
❯ what about other free tiers, whether vercel\netlify\render like or aws\gcp like??
The user is asking about the full landscape of free tier options including:
• Vercel, Netlify, Render (frontend/PaaS focused)
• AWS, GCP (major cloud providers)
• Others I might not have covered

Let me think about what each of these offers for CI/CD and self-hosted runner use cases:

Vercel: Free tier is excellent for frontend/Next.js/React but very limited for custom workloads. No persistent servers, no SSH access, no Docker. Good for deploying but not for self-hosted CI runners.

Netlify: Similar to Vercel - great for static sites, not for CI runners.

Render: Has "Free" tier with:
• Web services (auto-sleep after 15 min inactivity)
⠸ Analyzing 14s · Ctrl+C to interrupt              ⠧ Analyzing 14s · Ctrl+C to interrupt              ⠹ Analyzing 15s · Ctrl+C to interrupt              ^R
• Background workers (free for 90 days then paid)
• Cron jobs (free tier has limits)
• No SSH, no Docker on free tier
• Not suitable for persistent self-hosted runners

AWS:
• Free tier: 1 year only for most services
• EC2: 750 hours/month of t2.micro (but only for
  first year)
• CodeBuild: 100 min/month free (VERY limited for CI)
• After free tier: expensive
• EKS Fargate: expensive
• Lambda: not suitable for persistent workloads

GCP:
• Free tier: e2-micro (30GB SSD, 1GB RAM) forever
• Cloud Run: 2 million requests/month free, but cold
  starts
• Cloud Build: 120 min/month free (very limited)
• Compute Engine: Sustained use discounts but not
  free after year
• Cloud Functions: Event-driven, not persistent

Firebase: Hosting + functions, not for self-hosted runners

Heroku: No free tier anymore (retired in November 2022!)

Railway: $5 credit/month, spins down after inactivity, not truly persistent

Fly.io: 3 shared VMs with 256MB RAM each, better for edge functions than CI workloads. Supabase: Database and auth hosting, not CI runners. Neon: Serverless PostgreSQL, same limitations. Turso: SQLite edge database, unsuitable for this use case. Deno Deploy: Edge functions only. Cloudflare Workers: Serverless with generous free tier (100K requests/day), but not designed for persistent runners or Docker workloads.

The real constraint is that most modern PaaS and serverless platforms are optimized for ephemeral workloads or specific use cases, not for hosting self-managed infrastructure like CI runners that require persistent compute, Docker support, and SSH access.

For what's actually needed—persistent CI runners, Docker workloads, self-hosted runners, SonarQube, artifact storage, and nightly Snyk scans—only traditional VPS providers fit. Vercel, Netlify, Render, Railway, and Fly.io all fall short because they either lack SSH access, don't support Docker, spin down instances, or are too memory-constrained. AWS and GCP become cost-prohibitive quickly once free tiers expire. Oracle Cloud and Hetzner remain the practical choices at this scale.

## AWS vs GCP vs Oracle — Real Numbers

### AWS Free Tier (1 Year Only!)

┌───────────┬─────────────────┬──────────────────┐
│ Service   │ Free Tier       │ After 1 Year     │
├───────────┼─────────────────┼──────────────────┤
│ EC2       │ 750 hr/month    │ $8.47/mo         │
│ t2.micro  │                 │                  │
├───────────┼─────────────────┼──────────────────┤
│ CodeBuild │ 100 min/month   │ $0.003/min       │
│           │                 │ ($0.05/job)      │
├───────────┼─────────────────┼──────────────────┤
│ ECR       │ 500MB           │ $0.10/GB         │
├───────────┼─────────────────┼──────────────────┤
│ S3        │ 5GB             │ $0.023/GB        │
├───────────┼─────────────────┼──────────────────┤
│ RDS       │ 750 hr          │ $14.16/mo        │
│           │ (db.t2.micro)   │                  │
└───────────┴─────────────────┴──────────────────┘

Realistic post-free-tier cost for CI: $50-100/month minimum.

### GCP Free Tier (Forever e2-micro)

┌────────────────┬────────────┬──────────────────┐
│ Service        │ Free Tier  │ Notes            │
├────────────────┼────────────┼──────────────────┤
│ Compute        │ 1,600      │ Very slow (0.25  │
│ Engine         │ hours/mont │ vCPU burst)      │
│ e2-micro       │ h          │                  │
├────────────────┼────────────┼──────────────────┤
│ Cloud Build    │ 120        │ Completely       │
│                │ min/month  │ useless for CI   │
├────────────────┼────────────┼──────────────────┤
│ Cloud Run      │ 2M         │ Cold start       │
│                │ req/month  │ latency          │
├────────────────┼────────────┼──────────────────┤
│ Artifact       │ 0.5GB      │ Too small        │
│ Registry       │            │                  │
└────────────────┴────────────┴──────────────────┘

Problem: e2-micro is too slow for Rust/Go builds (1+ min just to spin up). Cloud Build's 120 min free tier is laughable — one Rust build is 3-5 min.

### Oracle Cloud Free (Forever)

┌─────────────────┬──────────────────────────────┐

│ Database        │ 1x Autonomous, 1GB storage   │
└─────────────────┴──────────────────────────────┘

This is legitimately the best free tier in cloud — 4 ARM cores with 24GB RAM is insane for free.

## The Honest Answer: Only Traditional VPS Works

For self-hosted CI runners, you need:

✅ SSH access
✅ Full Linux OS control
✅ Ability to install Docker
✅ Persistent storage
✅ No "spinning down" or sleep behavior
❌ Vercel/Netlify/Render/Railway don't provide t
  his

## Workers/Railway-style

Oracle Ampere (4 cores, 24GB RAM):
├─ TrueNAS Scale (NAS + Docker)
│   ├─ MinIO (S3-compatible artifact storage)
│   ├─ Watchtower (Docker updates)
│   └─ Custom apps (Snyk, coverage aggregator)
⠸ Analyzing 1:16m · Ctrl+C to interrupt            ├─ 1x Ubuntu VM (2 cores, 12GB RAM)
│   └─ Woodpecker CI server + 2 agents
└─ Kubernetes (k3s on remaining resources)

This gives you a "home cloud" that rivals $100/mo cloud setups — but on Oracle's free tier.

## For Your 100-500 PRs/Day Workload

### Minimum Viable ($10/mo)
Hetzner CX31 ($10) + Oracle Ampere (free)
  → 3-4 concurrent CI jobs
  → Good for ~30 repos at your PR volume

### Recommended ($20/mo)
Hetzner CX41 ($17) + Oracle Ampere (free)
  → 5-6 concurrent CI jobs
  → Handles ~60-80 repos at your PR volume
  → SonarQube on Oracle, CI on Hetzner

### High Volume ($40/mo)
Hetzner CX41 ($17) + Hetzner CX31 ($10)
  → 7-8 concurrent CI jobs
  → Full SonarQube on Oracle
  → Scales to your full 250 repo workload

## My Recommendation for You

Given your constraints (won't pay for GitHub Actions, 250 repos, 100-500 PRs/day):

### Phase 1: Free Tier
1. Oracle Cloud Ampere (free forever)
      ◦ Deploy SonarQube (4GB RAM minimum, 24GB available)
      ◦ PostgreSQL for artifact DB
      ◦ NFS share for Docker layers

### Phase 2: $10-20/mo
1. Hetzner CX31 ($10) for CI
      ◦ Woodpecker CI server + 2 agents
      ◦ Handles most PRs
      ◦ NVMe = fast Rust/Go builds
